50→ * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \"compact\" retention strategy.\n    51→ * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\n    52→ * <p>\n    53→ * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \"clean\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\n    54→ * \"dirty\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \"cleanable\" section followed by an \"uncleanable\" section.\n    55→ * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\n    56→ * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\n    57→ * <p>\n    58→ * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \"compact\" retention policy\n    59→ * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\n    60→ * <p>\n    61→ * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\n    62→ * the implementation of the mapping.\n    63→ * <p>\n    64→ * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\n    65→ * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\n    66→ * <p>\n    67→ * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\n    68→ * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\n    69→ * <p>\n    70→ * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\n    71→ * <p>\n    72→ * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\n    73→ * <p>\n    74→ * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\n    75→ * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\n    76→ * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\n    77→ * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\n    78→ * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\n    79→ * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\n    80→ * <p>\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. through a set of Java classes in the storage module. The core components are:\\n\\n**1. Cleaner Thread (LogCleaner.java):** The LogCleaner class is the main entry point for log compaction, implementing BrokerReconfigurable. It manages a pool of background CleanerThread instances (nested inner class that extends ShutdownableThread). Each CleanerThread continuously runs the doWork() method, which calls tryCleanFilthiestLog() and eventually cleanFilthiestLog() to perform log cleaning operations. The LogCleaner class is responsible for thread pool management, metrics collection, and configuration management.\\n\\n**2. Segment Selection Policy (LogCleanerManager.java):** LogCleanerManager implements the segment/log selection policy through the grabFilthiestCompactedLog() method. This method selects which log partition to clean next by computing a \\\"dirtiness\\\" ratio (the ratio of cleanable bytes to total bytes). It filters logs based on:\\n   - Whether they have compact retention policy enabled\\n   - Whether they are not already being cleaned\\n   - Whether they meet the minimum cleanable ratio threshold (minCleanableRatio from LogConfig)\\n   - Compaction lag timing constraints (min and max compaction lag)\\n\\nThe method uses a Comparator to find the \\\"filthiest\\\" log (highest cleanable ratio) and returns it as a LogToClean object. It also calculates cleanable offsets through the cleanableOffsets() method, which determines the first dirty offset and first uncleanable offset for each log.\\n\\n**3. Key-based Deduplication Logic (Cleaner.java with OffsetMap and SkimpyOffsetMap):** The actual key deduplication is implemented in the Cleaner class, which uses an OffsetMap (interface) backed by SkimpyOffsetMap (implementation). SkimpyOffsetMap is a memory-efficient hash table that:\\n   - Uses MD5 cryptographic hashing as a proxy for keys to save space\\n   - Stores key hashes and offset values in a ByteBuffer\\n   - Implements collision resolution through linear probing\\n   - Does not support deletions, only put() and get() operations\\n   - Tracks entries, lookups, and probes for statistics\\n\\nThe Cleaner.buildOffsetMap() method builds a complete key=>offset map for the dirty portion of a log by iterating through segments and calling buildOffsetMapForSegment(). This map represents the latest offset for each unique key in the dirty section. During cleanSegments(), the cleanInto() method recopies log segments while filtering out records whose keys appear in the offset map with higher offsets (i.e., removing obsolete records).\\n\\n**4. Supporting Components:**\\n   - **CleanerConfig.java:** Holds configuration parameters including thread count, IO buffer sizes, deduplication buffer size, and min/max compaction lag times\\n   - **LogToClean.java:** A helper class representing a log eligible for cleaning, with fields for topic partition, log reference, first dirty offset, cleanable bytes, and cleanable ratio\\n   - **PreCleanStats.java:** Collects pre-cleaning statistics like max compaction delay and number of cleanable partitions\\n   - **CleanerStats.java:** Tracks cleaning statistics including bytes/messages read and written, buffer utilization, and timing\\n   - **CleanedTransactionMetadata.java:** Handles transaction state tracking during cleaning, managing aborted and committed transactions to determine when control records can be safely removed\\n   - **LogCleaningState.java:** Defines state machine states for cleaning (InProgress, Aborted, Paused)\\n\\nThe complete flow is: CleanerThread.doWork() → grabFilthiestCompactedLog() (segment selection) → Cleaner.clean() → buildOffsetMap() (deduplication map building) → cleanSegments() → cleanInto() (key-based deduplication filtering).\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":524,"cache_read_input_tokens":52287,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":524},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f139a91e-073c-4a43-9195-67bb25a58768","uuid":"1e7be8ee-cb1c-47f8-b464-76fb3abd64ef"}

through a set of Java classes in the storage module. The core components are:\\n\\n**1. Cleaner Thread (LogCleaner.java):** The LogCleaner class is the main entry point for log compaction, implementing BrokerReconfigurable. It manages a pool of background CleanerThread instances (nested inner class that extends ShutdownableThread). Each CleanerThread continuously runs the doWork() method, which calls tryCleanFilthiestLog() and eventually cleanFilthiestLog() to perform log cleaning operations. The LogCleaner class is responsible for thread pool management, metrics collection, and configuration management.\\n\\n**2. Segment Selection Policy (LogCleanerManager.java):** LogCleanerManager implements the segment/log selection policy through the grabFilthiestCompactedLog() method. This method selects which log partition to clean next by computing a \\\"dirtiness\\\" ratio (the ratio of cleanable bytes to total bytes). It filters logs based on:\\n   - Whether they have compact retention policy enabled\\n   - Whether they are not already being cleaned\\n   - Whether they meet the minimum cleanable ratio threshold (minCleanableRatio from LogConfig)\\n   - Compaction lag timing constraints (min and max compaction lag)\\n\\nThe method uses a Comparator to find the \\\"filthiest\\\" log (highest cleanable ratio) and returns it as a LogToClean object. It also calculates cleanable offsets through the cleanableOffsets() method, which determines the first dirty offset and first uncleanable offset for each log.\\n\\n**3. Key-based Deduplication Logic (Cleaner.java with OffsetMap and SkimpyOffsetMap):** The actual key deduplication is implemented in the Cleaner class, which uses an OffsetMap (interface) backed by SkimpyOffsetMap (implementation). SkimpyOffsetMap is a memory-efficient hash table that:\\n   - Uses MD5 cryptographic hashing as a proxy for keys to save space\\n   - Stores key hashes and offset values in a ByteBuffer\\n   - Implements collision resolution through linear probing\\n   - Does not support deletions, only put() and get() operations\\n   - Tracks entries, lookups, and probes for statistics\\n\\nThe Cleaner.buildOffsetMap() method builds a complete key=>offset map for the dirty portion of a log by iterating through segments and calling buildOffsetMapForSegment(). This map represents the latest offset for each unique key in the dirty section. During cleanSegments(), the cleanInto() method recopies log segments while filtering out records whose keys appear in the offset map with higher offsets (i.e., removing obsolete records).\\n\\n**4. Supporting Components:**\\n   - **CleanerConfig.java:** Holds configuration parameters including thread count, IO buffer sizes, deduplication buffer size, and min/max compaction lag times\\n   - **LogToClean.java:** A helper class representing a log eligible for cleaning, with fields for topic partition, log reference, first dirty offset, cleanable bytes, and cleanable ratio\\n   - **PreCleanStats.java:** Collects pre-cleaning statistics like max compaction delay and number of cleanable partitions\\n   - **CleanerStats.java:** Tracks cleaning statistics including bytes/messages read and written, buffer utilization, and timing\\n   - **CleanedTransactionMetadata.java:** Handles transaction state tracking during cleaning, managing aborted and committed transactions to determine when control records can be safely removed\\n   - **LogCleaningState.java:** Defines state machine states for cleaning (InProgress, Aborted, Paused)\\n\\nThe complete flow is: CleanerThread.doWork() → grabFilthiestCompactedLog() (segment selection) → Cleaner.clean() → buildOffsetMap() (deduplication map building) → cleanSegments() → cleanInto() (key-based deduplication filtering).\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
